# PORT_OMISSIONS.md -- Python-reference symbols intentionally NOT implemented in signalwire-cpp

This file is checked by `scripts/enumerate_surface.py` +
`porting-sdk/scripts/diff_port_surface.py` on every PR. Every
Python-reference symbol missing from the C++ port MUST appear below with
a rationale, or the surface audit fails. See
`porting-sdk/CHECKLIST_TEMPLATE.md` section 13 "Symbol-level surface parity".

**Line format** -- one `<fully.qualified.symbol>: <reason>` per line. Blank
lines and Markdown-style headers/paragraphs are ignored by the parser.

## Rationale vocabulary

- `phone_binding` / `phone_binding_implicit`: covered by the phone-binding
  good path (`phone_numbers.set_*` helpers) per
  [porting-sdk/phone-binding.md](../porting-sdk/phone-binding.md). C++
  deliberately omits the legacy `assign_phone_route` path and the
  auto-materialized `create` endpoints on `SwmlWebhooksResource`,
  `CxmlWebhooksResource`, `AutoMaterializedWebhook`, and
  `CxmlApplicationsResource`.
- `serverless_out_of_scope`: C++ has no first-class Lambda/GCF/Azure
  runtime; custom-runtime-only deployment is out of scope per
  `porting-sdk/PORTING_GUIDE.md` Serverless Support section.
- `python_collapsed` / `python_collapsed_mixin`: Python's multiple
  inheritance fans methods out across mixin classes; C++ collapses them
  onto the concrete class. `scripts/enumerate_surface.py` projects
  implemented methods back to their mixin module so the diff matches.
  Remaining `python_collapsed_mixin` entries are mixin methods not yet
  implemented even on the collapsed class.
- `not_yet_implemented`: a future PR will implement this symbol. If one
  of these symbols becomes load-bearing for a real use case, file an
  issue and lift the rationale.

## Already-decided exemptions (phone-binding pivot)

These five lines carry forward the phone-binding precedent verbatim:

signalwire.rest.namespaces.fabric.GenericResources.assign_phone_route: narrow-use legacy API; C++ ships only the good path via phone_numbers.set_* helpers, per porting-sdk/phone-binding.md.
signalwire.rest.namespaces.fabric.SwmlWebhooksResource: phone-binding precedent: Python ships SwmlWebhooksResource as an indirection class with no methods of its own; C++ auto-materializes the same SWML webhook via phone_numbers.set_swml_webhook. The class is intentionally not exposed in C++ (there is nothing for the user to call directly).
signalwire.rest.namespaces.fabric.CxmlWebhooksResource: phone-binding precedent: Python ships CxmlWebhooksResource as an indirection class with no methods of its own; C++ auto-materializes the same cXML webhook via phone_numbers.set_cxml_webhook. The class is intentionally not exposed in C++ (there is nothing for the user to call directly).
signalwire.rest.namespaces.fabric.AutoMaterializedWebhook.create: phone-binding precedent: auto-materialized by phone_numbers.set_swml_webhook / set_cxml_webhook; C++ does not expose create.
signalwire.rest.namespaces.fabric.CxmlApplicationsResource.create: phone-binding precedent: C++ exposes phone_numbers.set_cxml_application(resource_id, application_id) instead; direct create on the resource is not exposed.

## Full symbol-level omissions

Every symbol below is missing in the C++ port relative to
`porting-sdk/python_surface.json`. Each line states the rationale.
Symbols above are not repeated.

signalwire.agent_server.AgentServer.get_agent: not_yet_implemented: Python AgentServer method names (get_agent/get_agents/register_global_routing_callback/serve_static_files/setup_sip_routing/register/unregister/register_sip_username) differ from the C++ equivalents (register_agent/unregister_agent/list_routes/set_static_dir/enable_sip_routing/map_sip_username). Python method-name aliases are not_yet_implemented.
signalwire.agent_server.AgentServer.get_agents: not_yet_implemented: Python AgentServer method names (get_agent/get_agents/register_global_routing_callback/serve_static_files/setup_sip_routing/register/unregister/register_sip_username) differ from the C++ equivalents (register_agent/unregister_agent/list_routes/set_static_dir/enable_sip_routing/map_sip_username). Python method-name aliases are not_yet_implemented.

signalwire.rest.namespaces.fabric.AutoMaterializedWebhook: not_yet_implemented: Python exposes a thin AutoMaterializedWebhook base that emits a DeprecationWarning when create() is called directly on swml_webhooks/cxml_webhooks. C++ ships swml_webhooks/cxml_webhooks as plain CrudResource-like fields with no deprecation hook. The C++ tests in test_rest_mock_fabric.cpp do not exercise this base; the canonical binding helpers live on phone_numbers (set_swml_webhook / set_cxml_webhook) and that path is fully covered.
signalwire.rest.namespaces.fabric.AutoMaterializedWebhook.create: not_yet_implemented: see AutoMaterializedWebhook above.

## Python instance attributes / properties not exposed in C++

Python's per-instance state attributes (`self.app`, `self.logger`, `self.skill_manager`, etc.) are exposed as Python @property descriptors and read via dot-access. The signature audit treats them as zero-arg getter methods. C++ does not expose these as public methods — they are private member fields owned by the class. The user-facing surface of the class is unchanged; users interact with the higher-level methods (`run`, `add_skill`, etc.) rather than reaching inside.

signalwire.agent_server.AgentServer.app: cpp_only: Python AgentServer.app exposes the underlying Flask/FastAPI app for advanced HTTP integration; C++ AgentServer uses httplib directly with no analogous app object to surface. End users reach HTTP customization via on_request / on_swml_request / register_route hooks instead.
signalwire.agent_server.AgentServer.logger: cpp_only: Python AgentServer.logger is a per-instance Python logging.Logger; C++ uses signalwire::logging::Logger which is module-level (no per-instance accessor). Equivalent functionality is reached via `signalwire::logging::get_logger("agent_server")`.
signalwire.core.agent_base.AgentBase.skill_manager: cpp_only: Python AgentBase.skill_manager exposes the SkillManager instance for advanced skill-loading workflows; C++ keeps SkillManager private and surfaces the same operations as AgentBase methods (add_skill, remove_skill, list_skills, has_skill).
signalwire.core.skill_base.SkillBase.logger: cpp_only: see AgentServer.logger — same module-level vs per-instance logger pattern.
signalwire.core.skill_manager.SkillManager.logger: cpp_only: see AgentServer.logger — same module-level vs per-instance logger pattern.
signalwire.core.swml_service.SWMLService.security: cpp_only: Python SWMLService.security exposes a per-service security/auth helper object; C++ folds the same operations (validate_basic_auth, get_basic_auth_credentials) directly onto SWMLService methods.
signalwire.core.swml_service.SWMLService.verb_registry: cpp_only: Python SWMLService.verb_registry is the verb-name-to-handler map exposed for inspection; C++ keeps the verb registry private and only exposes the user-facing verb operations (add_verb, has_function, etc.).
signalwire.skills.registry.SkillRegistry.logger: cpp_only: see AgentServer.logger — same module-level vs per-instance logger pattern.
